<div id="review_71632597" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/71632597" />
    <a title="Lizzie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1539362-lizzie"><img alt="Lizzie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1383432196p2/1539362.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/71632597?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lizzie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lizzie" href="/user/show/1539362-lizzie">Lizzie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781563892059" href="/book/show/437382.The_Sandman_Vol_9">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1539362-lizzie?shelf=fantasy-or-something">fantasy-or-something</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1539362-lizzie?shelf=2009">2009</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1539362-lizzie?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1539362-lizzie?shelf=myth">myth</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1539362-lizzie?shelf=david-s">david-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1539362-lizzie?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer71632597" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4378592612812995611">Well I just started reading this. Here is something about that. I won't even save it til I write the proper review, because, god.<br/><br/>F to this volume's introduction. F F F F F F it. There is the most giant spoiler in this introduction, and I didn't even read it. I'm so annoyed. It's just sitting there in a conspicuous spot on the page, and I think that's on purpose. I saw it as I flipped past and my jaw dropped, so then I stared at it, and ugh. This guy. It is just the most flippant and obnoxious wa</span>
  <span id="freeText4378592612812995611" style="display:none">Well I just started reading this. Here is something about that. I won't even save it til I write the proper review, because, god.<br /><br />F to this volume's introduction. F F F F F F it. There is the most giant spoiler in this introduction, and I didn't even read it. I'm so annoyed. It's just sitting there in a conspicuous spot on the page, and I think that's on purpose. I saw it as I flipped past and my jaw dropped, so then I stared at it, and ugh. This guy. It is just the most flippant and obnoxious way to drop a spoiler. <i>So there! NOW YOU KNOW. Isn't it just like Hamlet!?</i> <br /><br />It made turning the page to start the actual book into the saddest, crappiest feeling. SERIOUSLY. I preferred to PUT THE BOOK DOWN and come out here and RANT ON THE INTERNET, it made the start so sour. BAD JOB, dude.<br /><br />I don't know. I'm not trying to be a whiner and claim the experience is really "spoiled", but I am just not in the mood for it. It's the wrong type of story for this. Why not have the jaw drop at its appropriate time? Why not grapple with the idea when I know what it is for? You're forcing me to read it your way, and that sucks.<br /><br />If you want to compare it to Hamlet that is great. If you think it is awesome that the book ends the way it ends, THAT'S FANTASTIC. Then why don't you introduce Book 10! Or, I mean Book 7 didn't even have anything special happen and they moved the introduction to the end to preserve the story. I don't get it. A dick move.<br /><br />Anyway. Interested how this will shake out, but I wish it could just feel like a normal story I will probably like. Now it's all ANGSTY.<br /><br />Ha ha get it.<br /><br />.<br /><br />Well. My issues with the spoiler aside, this was a pretty good read. I think I'm going to let my thoughts on the ending simmer until I read the next book, so no spoilers, this time, from <i>me</i>.<br /><br />I'm having a small crisis because I really want to round this up to 4 stars, but I can't justify it. It's a really important part of the series, and it's long and a lot of interesting things are going on -- but also, a lot of it doesn't make sense. I don't exactly know what everyone was doing there, or even what actually happened or why. It might be enigma to unfold in the last volumes? But I feel like it's not.<br /><br />There was a nice best-of quality to the story. It was really, really nice to see Rose Walker again, who made Book 2 awesome awesome. (But I'm so annoyed with the issues drawn by the guy who makes her look like a softcore schoolgirl. What is up with them?) Also great to see Thessaly again, from Book 5 which I loved, matter-of-fact and fixing things up, but being really creepy about it. Not that I understood what she was doing? But hey.<br /><br />The main story with Hippolyta seeking her baby was ok, though in a familiar mold. The clue that something weird is going on, her occasional super-strength, isn't quite present enough to make me very interested, and I still don't quite understand it. The part with the Gorgons is neat. The Furies/Fates are ok. I guess it's all right to moosh them together into the same entities? I think that's what was up? Man this book was <i>unclear</i>.<br /><br />But I'm excited for the end of the series.</span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1121555331" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17303487212460903907">At more than 200 pages, this is the longest of the ten volume epic series, and pulls out all the stops to complete the story. I waited to write this review until after I finished the tenth and last volume, "The Wake," which I liked even better. This volume is about the variously named Furies, The Dirae, The Erinyes, the Eumenides: agents of vengeance, and if you see the final title, and you know who the series is basically about, well then you know the object of their vengeance and the result. I</span>
  <span id="freeText17303487212460903907" style="display:none">At more than 200 pages, this is the longest of the ten volume epic series, and pulls out all the stops to complete the story. I waited to write this review until after I finished the tenth and last volume, "The Wake," which I liked even better. This volume is about the variously named Furies, The Dirae, The Erinyes, the Eumenides: agents of vengeance, and if you see the final title, and you know who the series is basically about, well then you know the object of their vengeance and the result. In this tale we get a conclusion, in ambitious, operatic fashion, introduced and described beautifully by Frank McConnell. (I don't love all aspects of the introductions, which are typically too long, describe too much, and--this especially--spend altogether too much time deifying Gaiman as the single greatest contribution to comics and Literature itself EVER. Gaiman without question does make in this series one of the greatest contributions to comics and literature, but it makes one a little cynical to hear it page after page…intro after intro). <br /><br />In this volume (as with The Wake) you get visits from the principal cast of characters from all the volumes. The idea is to wrap things up, and end it as we know it must end, with gravitas and grace and lovely writing, and we get all that is promised. I don't like the artwork in this finish nearly as well as the work in The Wake. I do like the idea of having different artists doing the art throughout, and Dave McKean, who never draws the stories, doing all the covers. I like the idea of all these diverse contributions, even if I don't like all the unevenness of the styles. It gives one a sense of the variety of imagination, of the constructedness of the thing, as opposed to a sort of seamless artful tale.<br /><br />For all of its artful variation and power, not so much really happens in the last long volume except the unimpeded march of the Furies, Dream's creation of the Corinthian, a real nightmare, and revisiting all the characters we have met to end their individual tales. It's not as memorable as some of the other volumes, but it does essentially end the story and end it powerfully and quite neatly, Shakespearanly, with all things coming together, as a great epic series must end. For my money, though, The Wake is the greater ending to the series, the most moving, the most creative. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17303487212460903907" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4168667808590342856">The Kindly Ones was a rather large volume, but well worth it. It draws together many of the differing story arcs throughout the Sandman series.<br/><br/>The child, Daniel, is stolen by Loki. Loki convinces the idiot Lyta, blames Morpheus and sets into motion events that will have terrible consequences. Lyta brings in the Furies to destroy Morpheus, who has come under their purview for the killing of his son, Orpheus.<br/><br/>Meanwhile, this volume also draws to an end many of the unresolved story lines such as Clu</span>
  <span id="freeText4168667808590342856" style="display:none">The Kindly Ones was a rather large volume, but well worth it. It draws together many of the differing story arcs throughout the Sandman series.<br /><br />The child, Daniel, is stolen by Loki. Loki convinces the idiot Lyta, blames Morpheus and sets into motion events that will have terrible consequences. Lyta brings in the Furies to destroy Morpheus, who has come under their purview for the killing of his son, Orpheus.<br /><br />Meanwhile, this volume also draws to an end many of the unresolved story lines such as Cluracan, his sister and stories such as The Corinthian and Rose Walker.<br /><br />While I will nor ruin the ending, it could be said it is at once a finish and a new start to this story. A superb work of imagination, weaving in various mythologies to create a world of magic and dreams. I also truly enjoyed the inclusion of Lucifer and his views on Morpheus' plight. I see the basis for the superb Mike Carey "Lucifer" series here.<br /><br />If you've been following Sandman since the beginning, then this is a must read. Conversely, this is not the book to start this series with. Highly recommended, but read it in order of volume or you will be terribly confused.<br /><br />A work of art in terms of writing and the quality of the artwork.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14724865560063504758">A melancholy penultimate tale.<br/><br/>World: The art is great, it's atmospheric and sets the tone wonderfully. It's not the best in the series but it's still pretty great. The world building is phenomenal this time, this is the penultimate book and with it comes all the pieces that Gaiman has created for the Sandman series, it's a culmination of the world building and all the things he's created and set in motion for the entire run. Seeing them all interact to each other is absolutely amazing. <br/><br/>Story: Th</span>
  <span id="freeText14724865560063504758" style="display:none">A melancholy penultimate tale.<br /><br />World: The art is great, it's atmospheric and sets the tone wonderfully. It's not the best in the series but it's still pretty great. The world building is phenomenal this time, this is the penultimate book and with it comes all the pieces that Gaiman has created for the Sandman series, it's a culmination of the world building and all the things he's created and set in motion for the entire run. Seeing them all interact to each other is absolutely amazing. <br /><br />Story: The story is paced so well, the tone and the dialog is also amazing. There is a sense of melancholy to the story but it's sustained so well and handled so well. All the pieces that we've had on the run come together for this arc and it's astounding to see. The story I can't get into but the characters and their interaction and the slow boil of the story is what Sandman is known for and this is it. The finale, beautiful.<br /><br />Characters: Dream has been enigmatic since the start and all the enigmatic silent panels comes to an end here and we see where it leads. The Endless don't really have arcs, they are endless and ideas and somehow Gaiman was able to make Dream different since we first met him, this is the end of his arc and it's beautiful. The rest of the cast, I won't get into, the people we see this time around is amazing, all the pieces work together.<br /><br />This arc was amazing an culmination of ideas and characters Gaiman has created since Sandman #1.<br /><br />Onward to the next book!</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1130680137" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12227007000746004271">The ninth in the Sandman series gathers a number of threads, some started as far back as the second book in the series, and brings them to a conclusion. Morpheus is a stubborn character, someone who is not always prepared to compromise, and sometimes makes difficult choices. Characters from earlier books, including Hippolyta Hall, three witches, a Norse god and Thessaly are determined to settle those grudges<br/>But there is a cohesive and separate storyline in the book too. A child is taken, and the</span>
  <span id="freeText12227007000746004271" style="display:none">The ninth in the Sandman series gathers a number of threads, some started as far back as the second book in the series, and brings them to a conclusion. Morpheus is a stubborn character, someone who is not always prepared to compromise, and sometimes makes difficult choices. Characters from earlier books, including Hippolyta Hall, three witches, a Norse god and Thessaly are determined to settle those grudges<br />But there is a cohesive and separate storyline in the book too. A child is taken, and the mother thinks it is Morpheus and is set on destroying him. She turns to two ladies, The Kindly Ones, who she persuades to help her in this quest. Faced with the greatest challenge in his life, Morpheus confronts his foes and fears from a high and desolate peak surrounded and may have to make the greatest sacrifice yet.<br /><br />"It's never what they want, and if we give them what they think they want, they like it less than ever."<br /><br />The longest so far of the books, this is follows in the same vein as the last couple in the series, in that it has a set of stories that all hang together. Still dark though, but this time with an intensity and sinister and other worldly elements that make the hair on the back of your neck stand up. Sadly the artwork was not up to the quality of the previous books, not totally sure why, just lacked the detail. Other than that great book.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="12227007000746004271" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_998281972" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

<span id="freeTextContainer12275448174375496283">I can't even pretend that I got all of this. I'm not sure it's possible for anyone to get all of it in a single reading. Perhaps in the kind of intensive studying one associates with a doctoral thesis.   <span id="freeText12275448174375496283" style="display:none">I can't even pretend that I got all of this. I'm not sure it's possible for anyone to get all of it in a single reading. Perhaps in the kind of intensive studying one associates with a doctoral thesis. But even then only maybe.<br />Fun coincidence: I was reading this and also reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11504610.Hades_Lord_of_the_Dead__Olympians___4_" title="Hades Lord of the Dead (Olympians, #4) by George O'Connor" rel="nofollow noopener">Hades: Lord of the Dead</a>, because every time I got up some kid would swipe one of my books, and I'd have to switch to the other. Two books starring the Kindly Ones at once.<br />I'm starting to view Greek mythology the same way I view the tarot. Not as inherently meaningful, but as suggestive patterns that permit our own consciousnesses to make up the stories they need at the moment.<br />Library copy. (Although when I win the lottery, one of the first things I will do is buy the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23753.The_Absolute_Sandman__Volume_One" title="The Absolute Sandman, Volume One by Neil Gaiman" rel="nofollow noopener">The Absolute Sandman, Vol. 1</a> complete set. The second thing will be to build the library of my dreams in which they will reside)</span>
  <a data-text-id="12275448174375496283" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="&amp;#x1f341; Antonella &amp;#x1f341;" class="user" itemprop="url" name="&amp;#x1f341; Antonella &amp;#x1f341;" href="/user/show/7253042-x1f341-antonella-x1f341">&amp;#x1f341; Antonella &amp;#x1f341;</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7253042-x1f341-antonella-x1f341?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7253042-x1f341-antonella-x1f341?shelf=six-stars">six-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7253042-x1f341-antonella-x1f341?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7253042-x1f341-antonella-x1f341?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7253042-x1f341-antonella-x1f341?shelf=comics-graphic-novels">comics-graphic-novels</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3217429204" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18265852523249936220">WOW... just WOW. <br/><br/>I loved the previous volumes, but the stories on them at times felt loosely related and never seemed to lead anywhere. <br/>Now everything makes sense. <br/><br/>Lots of characters (if not all) we've seen throughout the series are back and the way all things tied up together and every single story lines wrapped up is brilliant. <br/><br/>This is hands down the best volume of <i>The Sandman</i> series and possibly the best comics volume out there. <br/></span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3488916741" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3488916741" />
    <a title="Ashley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley"><img alt="Ashley" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597876967p2/1343864.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3488916741?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ashley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ashley" href="/user/show/1343864-ashley">Ashley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781401291747" href="/book/show/43097811-the-sandman-vol-9">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=i-do-believe-in-fairies-i-do-i-do">i-do-believe-in-fairies-i-do-i-do</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=violent-and-epic">violent-and-epic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=folklore-and-mythology">folklore-and-mythology</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=graphic-novels-and-comics">graphic-novels-and-comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=speculative">speculative</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=what-s-this-art-thing-all-about-yo">what-s-this-art-thing-all-about-yo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1343864-ashley?shelf=horror">horror</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3488916741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6792930325361572369">I feel like I might be missing something here. I liked reading this but it wasn't my favorite of the Sandman comics, and I don't get the rapturous praise for it. I think some of my reaction may be again that I have read this series so spread out and I'm not making the connections with previous characters like I should. Some of it is also probably that it's not just vibrating on the right frequency for me. Shrug.<br/><br/>This is the climax, denouement of the story started back in the first volume. A bunch</span>
  <span id="freeText6792930325361572369" style="display:none">I feel like I might be missing something here. I liked reading this but it wasn't my favorite of the Sandman comics, and I don't get the rapturous praise for it. I think some of my reaction may be again that I have read this series so spread out and I'm not making the connections with previous characters like I should. Some of it is also probably that it's not just vibrating on the right frequency for me. Shrug.<br /><br />This is the climax, denouement of the story started back in the first volume. A bunch of threads (ha!) are tied together here as it all builds up to a quiet moment near the end of the book. It just didn't hit me very hard. (Another problem was that I didn't feel any sympathy for Lyta Hall. Her insistence that Morpheus was responsible for everything seemed delusional. I guess I just wanted a more righteous presence to play the role that she did, though her wrongness and incidental-ness in Dream's periphery seems to have been part of the point.)<br /><br />This volume was loooong. I think it might be the longest single comic volume I've ever read. I'm glad I didn't have to wait between issues; I would probably have lost patience with what would have felt like endless (ha!), pointless, drawn out conflict. <br /><br />I am saying very little about this drawn out volume, and feeling a little underwhelmed by the ending to this story. Apparently #10 is more of an epilogue.<br /><br />Oh, well. Maybe I will feel differently on re-read. Next time I'm definitely reading all the volumes back to back.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6792930325361572369" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('WH4lRlxm0YUIFncSHDZwWP0/ZRd91MUyykpHLXWPEBls2LkrLYVYXNcmcFs0ZzfYFLaqW82uNeCCDsxfIj4/Jg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dYfBbKP7mgcltZi+DOjRetkg6JK90HNsn7slLt7IqL1BIV0B0hgT3vqFn/ckuZb6MKkn3g2qg77X/65ciXmHgg==')})
  }
//]]>

They don't teach you how to be rich or how to be poor. They don't teach you how to walk away from someone you don't love any longer. They don't teach you how to know what's going on in someone else's mind. They don't teach you what to say to someone who's dying. They don't teach you anything worth knowing.&rdquo;</span>
